18.1.2 Visualization of Results

Let us apply the resamples() function from {caret} to the list of models, to get metrics computed on the final model produced by the train() function from {caret}, i.e., the model which provided the best performances with respect to sensitivity on the validation sets (computed over the repeated 5-fold cross validation, see Chapter 17). Since we performed 10 repetitions of 5-fold cross validation, the metrics are computed on 10*5=50 validation samples.

list_models <- list(
  rf = grid_search_rf,
  xgb = grid_search_xgb,
  svm = svm_model,
  glmnet = glmnet_model
)
results <- resamples(list_models)

We can have a look at a summary of the results. The summary function we used was twoClassSummary(). This function returns three metrics: ROC-AUC, sensitivity, and specificity. For each repetition and each fold, we thus have a value for these three metrics computed on the validation sample.

summary(results)

For each of the models, we can look at the performance metrics computed on the validation samples for the best set of hyperparameters.

bwplot(results)

Let us load the train and test samples (defined in Chapter 5):

load("../data/out/df_train_sah.rda")
load("../data/out/df_test_sah.rda")
ind_remove <- which(
  colnames(df_train) %in% c("status", "id", "PERSONNE_statut")
)

For each model, let us compute some additional metrics on the train and on the test set. We need to load the packages required to make predictions using the fitted models.

Then, we can loop over the models and compute the predictions on both the train set and the test set. For each set, we focus on the accuracy, the sensitivity, and on the specificity.

res_train <- NULL
res_test <- NULL
roc_curves <- NULL
for (mod in list_models) {
  # Predictions
  pred_train <- predict(mod, newdata = df_train[,-ind_remove])
  pred_test <- predict(mod, newdata = df_test[-ind_remove])
  # Predicted scores
  pred_train_scores <- predict(
    mod, newdata = df_train[,-ind_remove], type = "prob"
  )
  pred_test_scores <- predict(
    mod, newdata = df_test[,-ind_remove], type = "prob"
  )
  # Confusion matrices
  cm_train <- confusionMatrix(pred_train, df_train$status)
  cm_test <- confusionMatrix(pred_test, df_test$status)
  # ROC Curves
  roc_train <- MLeval::evalm(
    data.frame(pred_train_scores, df_train$status), 
    showplots = FALSE
  )
  ind_roc_train <- which(row.names(roc_train$stdres$Group1) == "AUC-ROC")
  roc_val_train <- roc_train$stdres$Group1$Score[ind_roc_train]
  roc_test <- MLeval::evalm(
    data.frame(pred_test_scores, df_test$status), 
    showplots = FALSE
  )
  ind_roc_test <- which(row.names(roc_test$stdres$Group1) == "AUC-ROC")
  roc_val_test <- roc_test$stdres$Group1$Score[ind_roc_test]
  
  # Binding the results
  res_train <- bind_rows(
    res_train, 
    tibble(
      method = mod$method, 
      accuracy = cm_train$overall["Accuracy"],
      sensitivity = cm_train$byClass[c("Sensitivity")],
      specificity = cm_train$byClass[c("Specificity")],
      auc = roc_val_train
    )
  )
  res_test <- bind_rows(
    res_test, 
    tibble(
      method = mod$method,
      accuracy = cm_test$overall["Accuracy"],
      sensitivity = cm_test$byClass[c("Sensitivity")],
      specificity = cm_test$byClass[c("Specificity")],
      auc = roc_val_test
    )
  )
  # And for the roc curves
  roc_curves <- bind_rows(
    roc_curves,
    roc_train$roc$data |> mutate(model = mod$method, sample = "train") |> 
    bind_rows(
      roc_test$roc$data |> mutate(model = mod$method, sample = "test")
    )
  )
}

The performances metrics are shown in Table 18.1.

Code 
library(kableExtra)
res_train |> mutate(sample = "Train") |> 
  bind_rows(
    res_test |> mutate(sample = "Test")
  ) |> 
  mutate(sample = factor(sample, levels = c("Train", "Test"))) |> 
  pivot_wider(
    names_from = "sample", 
    values_from = c("accuracy", "sensitivity", "specificity", "auc")
  ) |> 
  kable(
    align=c('l', rep('c', 7)), digits = 3, 
    col.names = c("Method", rep(c("Train", "Test"), 4))
  ) |> 
  kable_styling("striped") %>%
  add_header_above(
    c(" " = 1, "Accuracy" = 2, "Sensitivity" = 2, "Specificity" = 2, "AUC" = 2)
  )

The ROC curves:

Code 
source("../Codes/utils.R")
plot_roc_curves <- ggplot(
  data = roc_curves |> 
    mutate(
      model = factor(
        model, 
        levels = c("ranger", "xgbTree", "svmRadial", "glmnet"),
        labels = c(
          "Random Forest", "XGBoost", "SVM", "Penalized Logistic Regression"
        )
      ),
      sample = factor(
        sample, 
        levels = c("train", "test"), 
        labels = c("Train", "Test")
      )
    ), 
  mapping = aes(x = FPR, y = SENS, colour = model, linetype = model)) +
  geom_line() +
  scale_colour_manual(NULL, values = c(
    "Random Forest" = "#009E73", 
    "XGBoost" = "#D55E00", 
    "SVM" = "#56B4E9", 
    "Penalized Logistic Regression" = "#CC79A7"
  )) +
  scale_linetype_discrete(NULL) +
  theme_paper() +
  labs(x = "False positive rate", y = "True positive rate") +
  facet_wrap(~sample)
